# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Rust Trait Solver Obligation Chain

## Your Task

## Context

{"content":"1: //! The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \"backtrace\" of each\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\n5: //! place).\n6: //!\n7: //! ### External view\n8: //!\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\n11: //!\n12: //! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\n13: //! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\n14: //!\n15: //! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\n16: //! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\n17: //! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\n24: //!\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Perfect! I've created a comprehensive `answer.json` file that traces the trait obligation chain in the Rust compiler. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings:

**Core Components:**
1. **ObligationForest** - The foundational data structure that tracks outstanding trait obligations in a tree structure
2. **FulfillmentContext** - Orchestrates the obligation resolution process using the ObligationForest
3. **FulfillProcessor** - The processor that drives obligation fulfillment with SelectionContext
4. **SelectionContext** - The heart of trait selection that determines if obligations can be satisfied

**Trait Selection Pipeline:**
1. **Candidate Assembly** (`assemble_candidates` and `assemble_candidates_from_impls`) - Collects all possible impl candidates that could satisfy an obligation
2. **Impl Matching** (`MatchAgainstFreshVars`) - Tests whether an impl header can be unified with the obligation
3. **Confirmation** (`confirm_candidate`) - Confirms the selected candidate and returns the impl source

**Error Reporting:**
1. **FulfillmentError** - Encapsulates obligation failures with error codes
2. **report_selection_error** - Handles specific error scenarios with context-aware messages
3. **report_fulfillment_errors** - The main entry point that generates user-facing error messages

The answer file includes:
- 10 critical source files
- 16 key symbols implementing the system
- A 10-step ordered chain showing the data flow
- Detailed narrative explaining the complete obligation resolution process

Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\\n13: //! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\\n14: //!\\n15: //! This tree is a singleton to start, so\\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\\n24: //!\\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\\n26: //!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\\n27: //!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\\n28: //!   surrounding environment changes.\\n29: //! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\\n30: //!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\\n31: //!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\\n32: //!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \\\"true\\\"\\n33: //!   success if `C` is empty. No further\\n41: //!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\\n42: //!   now considered to be in error.\\n43: //!\\n44: //!     "content": "1: //! The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \"backtrace\" of each\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\n5: //! place).\n6: //!\n7: //! ### External view\n8: //!\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\n11: //!\n12: //! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\n13: //! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\n14: //!\n15: //! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\n16: //! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\n17: //! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\n24: //!\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\n26: //!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\n27: //!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\n28: //!   surrounding environment changes.\n29: //! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\n30: //!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\n31: //!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\n32: //!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \"true\"\n33: //!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\n34: //!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\n35: //!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\n36: //!   `process_obligations`.\n37: //! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\n38: //!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\n39: //!   \"backtrace\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\n40: //!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\n41: //!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\n42: //!   now considered to be in error.\n43: //!\n44: //! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\n45: //! which includes two bits of information:\n46: //!\n47: //! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\n48: //!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\n49: //!   have also been completed). So, for example, if the callback from\n50: //!   `process_obligations` returns `Changed(C)` for some obligation `O`,\n51: ",

structure and selection algorithm. Here's how trait obligations are resolved:\\n\\n## 1. ObligationForest - Core Data Structure\\nThe foundation of the trait obligation system is the `ObligationForest` (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs). This utility data structure tracks outstanding trait obligations that haven't yet been resolved. Obligations form a tree structure where each obligation can have sub-obligations. The forest processes obligations and returns outcomes with completed obligations and errors.\\n\\nThe `ObligationForest` uses a generic `ForestObligation` trait to allow different obligation types. `PendingPredicateObligation` is the concrete implementation used in trait selection, defined in compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs.\\n\\n## 2. FulfillmentContext - Orchestrating Obligation Resolution\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs) drives the trait resolution process. It wraps an `ObligationForest<PendingPredicateObligation>` and provides methods to:\\n- Register new root obligations\\n- Process obligations through the forest\\n- Return fulfillment errors for unsatisfied obligations\\n\\nDuring the fulfillment process, the `FulfillProcessor` (a struct implementing `ObligationProcessor`) works with a `SelectionContext` to process each obligation.\\n\\n## 3. Trait Selection - SelectionContext\\nThe `SelectionContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs) is responsible for determining whether a trait obligation can be satisfied. It orchestrates the entire selection process with the following steps:\\n\\n### 3a. Candidate Assembly (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs)\\nThe `assemble_candidates` method collects all possible candidates that could satisfy a trait obligation:\\n- `assemble_candidates_from_impls` - searches for matching trait impls in the codebase\\n- `assemble_candidates_from_caller_bounds` - checks where-clause bounds\\n- `assemble_builtin_copy_clone_candidate` - for builtin traits like Copy and Clone\\n- Other specialized candidate assembly methods for specific lang items\\n\\n### 3b. Impl Matching (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs)\\nThe `MatchAgainstFreshVars` struct implements matching logic that tests whether an impl header can be unified with the obligation. Matching involves:\\n- Replacing bound regions in the obligation with placeholders\\n- Unifying the impl header with the obligation\\n- Checking for placeholder leaks (where placeholders relate to non-impl regions)\\n\\n### 3c. Candidate Confirmation (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs)\\nOnce a candidate is selected, `confirm_candidate` confirms it and returns:\\n- The impl source (UserDefined, Builtin, etc.)\\n- Any nested obligations required by the impl\\n\\n## 4. Error Reporting - Unsatisfied Trait Bounds\\nWhen trait obligations cannot be satisfied, error reporting occurs through:\\n\\n### 4a. Error Types (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/mod.rs)\\n`FulfillmentError` combines:\\n- The obligation that failed\\n- `FulfillmentErrorCode` which can be:\\n  - `Select(SelectionError)` - trait selection failed (Unimplemented is primary error)\\n  - `Project(MismatchedProjectionTypes)` - associated type mismatch\\n  - `Ambiguity` - multiple possible solutions\\n\\n### 4b. Error Reporting Pipeline (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs)\\nThe `report_selection_error` method handles different error scenarios:\\n- For `SelectionError::Unimplemented` - trait not implemented for the type\\n- Provides specific context from well-formedness checking\\n- Generates helpful suggestions for common mistakes\\n\\n### 4c. Main Error Reporter (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs)\\nThe `report_fulfillment_errors` method in `TypeErrCtxt` is the entry point for reporting all trait bound errors. It processes multiple errors and coordinates with suggestion providers to give users helpful guidance.\\n\\n## End-to-End Flow\\n1. Obligations are registered in `FulfillmentContext`\\n2. `process_obligations` is called on the `ObligationForest`\\n3. `FulfillProcessor` works with `SelectionContext` for each obligation\\n4. `assemble_candidates` collects all possible trait impl matches\\n5. `MatchAgainstFreshVars` determines if impls match the obligation\\n6. Successful matches are confirmed, returning nested obligations\\n7. Unfulfillable obligations become errors\\n8. `report_fulfillment_errors` generates user-facing error messages with suggestions\\n\\nThis architecture ensures efficient trait obligation resolution while providing detailed error messages when traits cannot be satisfied.\"\n}\n",

Trait Selection - SelectionContext\\nThe `SelectionContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs) is responsible for determining whether a trait obligation can be satisfied. It orchestrates the entire selection process with the following steps:\\n\\n### 3a. Candidate Assembly (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs)\\nThe `assemble_candidates` method collects all possible candidates that could satisfy a trait obligation:\\n- `assemble_candidates_from_impls` - searches for matching trait impls in the codebase\\n- `assemble_candidates_from_caller_bounds` - checks where-clause bounds\\n- `assemble_builtin_copy_clone_candidate` - for builtin traits like Copy and Clone\\n- Other specialized candidate assembly methods for specific lang items\\n\\n### 3b. Impl Matching (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs)\\nThe `MatchAgainstFreshVars` struct implements matching logic that tests whether an impl header can be unified with the obligation. Matching involves:\\n- Replacing bound regions in the obligation with placeholders\\n- Unifying the impl header with the obligation\\n- Checking for placeholder leaks (where placeholders relate to non-impl regions)\\n\\n### 3c. Candidate Confirmation (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs)\\nOnce a candidate is selected, `confirm_candidate` confirms it and returns:\\n- The impl source (UserDefined, Builtin, etc.)\\n- Any nested obligations required by the impl\\n\\n## 4. Error Reporting - Unsatisfied Trait Bounds\\nWhen trait obligations cannot be satisfied, error reporting occurs through:\\n\\n### 4a. Error Types (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/mod.rs)\\n`FulfillmentError` combines:\\n- The obligation that failed\\n- `FulfillmentErrorCode` which can be:\\n  - `Select(SelectionError)` - trait selection failed (Unimplemented is primary error)\\n  - `Project(MismatchedProjectionTypes)` - associated type mismatch\\n  - `Ambiguity` - multiple possible solutions\\n\\n### 4b. Error Reporting Pipeline (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs)\\nThe `report_selection_error` method handles different error scenarios:\\n- For `SelectionError::Unimplemented` - trait not implemented for the type\\n- Provides specific context from well-formedness checking\\n- Generates helpful suggestions for common mistakes\\n\\n### 4c. Main Error Reporter (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs)\\nThe `report_fulfillment_errors` method in `TypeErrCtxt` is the entry point for reporting all trait bound errors. It processes multiple errors and coordinates with suggestion providers to give users helpful guidance.\\n\\n## End-to-End Flow\\n1. Obligations are registered in `FulfillmentContext`\\n2. `process_obligations` is called on the `ObligationForest`\\n3. `FulfillProcessor` works with `SelectionContext` for each obligation\\n4. `assemble_candidates` collects all possible trait impl matches\\n5. `MatchAgainstFreshVars` determines if impls match the obligation\\n6. Successful matches are confirmed, returning nested obligations\\n7. Unfulfillable obligations become errors\\n8. `report_fulfillment_errors` generates user-facing error messages with suggestions\\n\\nThis architecture ensures efficient trait obligation resolution while providing detailed error messages when traits cannot be satisfied.\"\n}\n",
